Howard Kui</name>
<Date>1512547359294</Date><Rating>1<//Rating>< Text>
This review is for AAA Travel. I received great service during the inquiry and booking process for our cruise to Alaska, but sadly service went drastically downhill, conveniently once we had fully paid and it was non-refundable, so beware! My family has been AAA members for over 40 years, and used AAA Travel for many years, but I'd rather book all my cruises and other travel online or with another agency than use AAA Travel going forward!

We were looking to book a cruise to Alaska, so I researched online and found AAA Travel which had competitive rates with extras such as additional onboard credits and a bottle of champagne for each cabin. I called and was put in touch with their travel counselor, Amber Smith, in the Richmond-Hilltop office. It started out great. She was very nice, prompt in answering all my questions, and providing various quotes, which led to booking our reservation.

Everything was going great, until she made a mistake by forgetting to pay our final payment and our booking was canceled as a result! When she realized her mistake, she reassured me she fixed everything and was able to rebook us to the way it was before, which to me meant same cabin, same fare, onboard credits, etc. However, to my disappointment, once we made our final payment and received the final confirmation, everything had changed- our cabins, our dining time, increase in fare, and we lost $50 per cabin in onboard credits!

All of a sudden she became less responsive to my emails and phone calls, and she kept giving me the run around. If she had simply acknowledged her mistake (she tried to blame me initially saying that I didn't notify her, but I have an email proving I did), sincerely apologized, and made it a priority to fix it, but was unsuccessful, I might have let it go. Instead, all I got was one excuse after another, placing blame on what seemed like one thing after another. The branch manager, Paul Mulig, overheard my heated tone and our discussion when I paid her a visit in person and tried to assure me that he would try to help her to get this resolved. It started looking promising, but unfortunately it ended up being no help. Just before our cruise, Amber claimed to have fixed it, by purchasing a gift certificate or onboard credit of some sort for us to use on board the cruise, but at the same time she was being extremely vague and unclear as to how or when we would get it.

To no surprise, when we got on board, we saw no sign of that gift certificate nor any additional onboard credits. The extra bottle of wine she also promised us was nowhere to be seen. She then blamed her rep at Royal Caribbean. If we did believe her, then her rep has definitely made her look bad. If I were her, I would have escalated the issue at Royal Caribbean, but judging from her actions up to this point, she didn't seem to try at all for us. Although Amber is a very nice person, as a "experienced" travel counselor she never showed she was proactive, never did any follow up without me asking her to, and never gave me a sense of any priority or urgency on making this right.

Now it is over 3 months since we've come back from our cruise and still no resolution! I have not received any follow up or update from Amber or Paul. Unbelievable. I've worked in client services for a CPA firm for many years as a successful accountant and business consultant. I was always assigned the high profile clients, because I was one of the best at providing customer service. Whenever I made a mistake, it would be one of my top priorities to work on it until I got the issue resolved, and never hesitated to escalate any issues with any 3rd parties. No excuses. Period.

I am deeply disappointed with this experience, as there is NO excuse for any of this to dragged out this long. I will never use Amber and AAA Travel again!< /Text>

<text>I booked a flight for my sisters birthday. They picked us up at Pier 39 and then tour before the tour begann. Paul our driver was really nice and explained all the places we passed. And we even got to drive over the Golden Gate Bridge.
Arrived we were welcomed very friendly. The seaplane with our pilot Aron awaited us already. He was great, very funny and polite. He explained everything to us and even talked to us in pretty good German. We felt totally safe. We were lucky and the only ones on board.

<rating>3<//rating><review>Beautiful setting, decent service and some hits and misses when it comes to the food.

It's obvious why so many rave about the gorgeous setting, especially at night with the outdoor lights. Thai night did not disappoint, except maybe the crowd. It was the 15th of February, so there may have been some carry over from Valentines which typically makes great restaurants ordinary due to the kitchen being overwhelmed. Same goes with service. At times I felt rushed and out of place and other times treated as expected in a high end restaurant. I guess only another visit during a typical dinner service will tell.

As for the food, the Rack of lamb was delish but why call it a rack when it was just chops? The braised beef cheeks were not our fave, but ok. Same for the Red beet salad. We were very disappointed in the Spanish octopus cocktail. It was like a bad version of a typical octopus cocktail at a mariscos restaurant. I only wish i had tapatio to add some extra flavor. The real winner and highlight of the night was the Grand Marnier Souffl√©. That did not disappoint, neither did the "show"<//review><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMRZrTfYHZpt4PcmINeytrRH-rxnl0b7w8gTtPy=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPudDyPqwF6ixH6MHqa7Rp5URyC8Bv-qpkBiuK-=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP8UEAil8Ak4aKA7XgKaFIE1aB8xlM5_cS8ajHh=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMzoYfROCMxCNoSTPnCvadsbRWz9p5qMAhVQ2pN=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPXf-z9aFJKyitPT35mkcGCABrahEUp35h1pCX5=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOc4cdCm0UPu8UjEM3MxtLI69vXxzMtHG6KXlRC=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMpwckvUXXcfjN_zdLXRsUoMhRHHJf-REEB0PsJ=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOqtitdnITZqVZmnWYD8hPxNvCO-LO5c_AX7l1p=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNT4TzH7XY0XAhWonCvGRiVJfUsABaH3OtIOlRL=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPkIcRTJlHClvUvW2QLp4hUwalu7ZWG-dOiGLSP=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNpLDY9qgNKbr8HIr27NpLWaAL25LcFDnfTIkjI=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipM2RQc5gIPcJFYyuMuizEa6VEj_RbS4u9CI55TT=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOWYXN6SImsCn76vai90CebJbFYfsved5Cb4_IE=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pics><resp>None< /resp>< gmapID>

Very underwhelming experience for Palm Springs Restaurant Week. The menu was a poor value compared to many of the other places I‚Äôve gotten to try this week, and I was pretty shocked at the lack of flavor in the food.

All three courses were bland as can be, unexciting, and lacking any texture - everything was a different form of mush. In all fairness their demographic was very old... we were definitely the only people below 50 in the restaurant, so that probably suits their target market. Most of the food was not remotely French either, which was a pretty big letdown.

Maybe their regular menu is decent, but based on this experience I cannot recommend this establishment. Impeccable service, as our server was pleasant and attentive - but that did not make up for the subpar dining experience.<//review>

<Rate>1<//Rate>< Review>
Where to begin? I had heard nothing but great things about this French restaurant. I was really excited to enjoy amazing food with 4 of my best friends on the last day of the year. We were lucky to get a reservation (we thought) and our taste buds would be exploding with amazing flavors.
From the moment we walked in, we were met with an overcrowded entrance/lobby which was surprising to me. I thought we had a reservation to start enjoying dinner at 845. Instead, we were moved into the bar area where a band was setting up and a dance floor, which was overcrowded with others waiting to be seated as well.
We had to seek someone out from the restaurant in order to get a table after waiting almost an hour. That is not what you expect from an upscale locale. Once seated, we were surprised to discover that there was a pre-fixe menu with a cost of $160 per person. Having prior fine dining experience I wasn‚Äôt thrown off by the price, as long as the food was up to par.
After placing our orders we each enjoyed our appetizers and the excitement was increasing for me, a great meal was about to be enjoyed.
That‚Äôs where it went all wrong. Our waitress and her assistant started putting spoons out as cutlery for our next dish. We thought perhaps a pleasant surprise was in store, perhaps a nice French bisque soup or something exciting.
Instead, our deserts were brought out. We all stopped the waitress and let her know we had yet to receive our main dishes. I had ordered the Branzino however when it came, I smelled it and immediately knew it had sat too long or was not fresh. We asked if we could exchange it for another item. We were able to exchange it for the lobster.
Sadly, the lobster (3 of which where ordered by our table) was cold. That is unacceptable in a restaurant of this caliber. I took one or two bites and just left it, I was not about to go down that slippery slope of suffering through a bad dish. My other friend ordered chateaubriand and she was also surprised at the coldness of the temperature. Now I was upset that the restaurant we had been looking forward to all weekend was underdelivering on expectations.
The meal ended with a subpar dessert, in which the main waitress had to correct the direction of the placement of the dessert.
Before leaving I requested to speak with the manager, which never happened. Instead, we were given the on lobster off at market price ($48). I did make a call the following day and spoke with the manager, who let the owner know and he would be calling me back.
The result of the call was as follows: nobody else complained about the evening and the pre-fixe price included entertainment (band), dancing and party favors. They don‚Äôt like to rush people so if we were expecting to be in and out they apologize for that experience. However, they have been having this event for the past 45 years. I guess we should know their history, despite this being our very first visit to the restaurant. He was unwilling to credit or offer a discount for our experience (nearly a $900 meal) but rather offer a complimentary bottle of champagne upon our next visit.
No thank you, this place is dated and the way things are dealt with in a service industry that relies on reputation lets me know that we are not the caliber of diners they host. I sure wish I had a different experience. I will let any person who asks about this restaurant to steer way clear.
Not impressed, extremely underwhelmed and absolutely offended.<//Review>

<Rate>2< /Rate><Text>We received a gift certificate worth $150 towards what we thought would be a fine dining experience at Le Vallauris. Note, onsite parking is very limited, with "valet" service available, we opted for street parking and walked the few steps to the front door.

Our host must've been tired - his less than enthusiastic greeting, coupled with a mechanical "follow me", made us think back to a crabby greeter at a Denny's  (apologies to Denny's). With no eye contact, he mumbled something unintelligible, weaving his way towards the back patio seating area.

Plenty of seating for two was available, but despite being well-dressed we felt like our back wall seating missed the mark (see photos).

A magic marker style menu on an easel was plopped down with scribbled specials (no notes re accompaniments or sides), followed by a fixed price, two choice menu. Passed on that.

Our waitress was cheerful and attentive but somehow a couple that showed up after us received their appetizers first.

We shared the escargot, my wife had a delicious and well-prepared filet mignon $43.00, I had the passable .5lb (after shelling) saut√©ed lobster $48.00. A half-ish glass of red or white wine will set you back $14 - $18 each. Various meh greens on a bed of doughy something finished the plating.

Sadly, Le Vallauris has probably seen better days - indicated by the faded TripAdvisor and other gradings posted at the front entrance.

Tucked away in a vintage residential area, the eateries on Palm Canyon, a couple of blocks away, might provide more for a gift certificate.</Text><username>xfirehurican<//username>< Response>
None<//Response>

<Text>If you want a place where you can buy just about any Cuban food product this is the place.HOWEVER, beware!! This place uses that very ancient system of charging. The put a very flimsy little sticker on the products with the price of the item. When the cashier begins to charge you, they add cents and even dollars to the item. For example an item has that little sticker for $2.49 but the cashiers types in, very fast mind you, $2.99. On a large purchase, this adds up to dollars in total. If they notice that you are trusting and not even paying attention, like me, they really stick it to you...!

Just now I arrived home from a purchase with them, wondering why my bill was so high. Every time I go there my bill is way higher than I guesstimated. I mean way higher. Finally I became suspicious, something that I never do. I checked my itemized bill against all the products purchased. And indeed...! They had over charged me $12.53, using the very method I explained above. And I guess this dude at the register really saw me gullible, because he rang up an item for $7.99. The highest price item I purchased was suppose to be only $5.49.

Also, watch out with the expiration dates, especially items in the freezer. Like the "croquettas," just about all of them have no expiration date. This is a major violation with the U.S. Department of Health. Always reach for items in the very back of the freezer.

I highly recommend when you go buy there, bring a calculator with you. And as you put items in your cart, add them up. If an item does not have a price on it, ask! Don't trust them! Believe me, these type of people have a history in Cuba... and is not a good one. They are shady crooks!< /Text>< Pictures>

< Text>
Since starting school at UCSC, I‚Äôve been a regular here along with friends. The staff work so hard and send out meals as soon as they can. So far, I‚Äôve enjoyed all of the meals I‚Äôve ordered (my family is Chinese and we frequently eat home cooked Chinese food, so I‚Äôll vouch for the decency of this Chinese takeout). They also have plenty of vegan options that are just as delicious as the other menu items. The veggie buns are a must (vegans or non vegans!)! Fluffy with a perfect mushroom filling. One time I accidentally ordered something incorrectly and the owner quickly made me a new batch with no charge at closing time (even though I tried my best to pay), which I am extremely grateful for. They make me want to order from them because they treat their customers well and I trust them to always give a quality meal! Food is also great when packaged for takeout. They separate the sauce from some dishes to prevent sogginess so I can reheat it at home. Definitely worth a try! Especially now, takeout is crucial for these restaurants. Support the community if you can!< /Text>

< Review>
I took a chance and ordered online delivery for my first meal with Shun Feng. I ordered cucumber salad, soup dumplings, mu shu shrimp and shrimp shu mai. Firstly, it took them MAYBE 20 minutes from the time I ordered to when the deliver guy showed up at my door, so that was cool. But also, they left me a note on my order that I was outside their normal delivery zone (the website still let me??) but to please pick up next time. I thought that was so nice of them!! Now on to the food... The cucumber salad was delicious, the soup dumplings were decent (probably not the best choice for delivery on my part since they were luke warm upon arrival and I tried to steam them again, poor idea), shrimp shu mai was pretty standard but guys, the mu shu shrimp was the star here. I have never had such fresh mu shu! I was expecting it to be oily, soaked in sauce, mushy but tasty (aka a standard Chinese takeout mu shu) but instead the cabbage was tender, the shrimp were plump and there was no sopping sauce, just a perfect amount of delicate broth! I have tried three other Chinese restaurants here in the area and I can honestly say Shun Feng is at the top. I am currently reordering for dinner right now! But for pick up ;)

Review edit - the Wor Wonton soup is the best wonton soup I‚Äôve ever had. It is so flavorful and comforting. I will be back for more as these days get cooler!!</Review>

< Review>
While the service was fast, my vegetables were virtually raw and my shrimp had a disturbingly mushy texture coupled with an awful, fishy taste. The corn in our veggies also had an off texture, was grayish in color, and tasted like an old can. We also had the salad (a giant piece of lettuce with this clear, thin, super sweet and oddly sour 'dressing') and soup of the day, hot and sour soup, and it had nasty canned peas in it.
Everything was dirty. My fork had caked on, old and dry food, my cup also had some black things stuck to the inside, and there were bits of hardened rice under the lip of my plate.
There was no filter for the tea that we ordered, so we were having to pick out sticks and leaves every time we poured a cup.
Seaweed was mixed into all of the vegetables, which, while it's not necessarily a complaint, for the dishes we ordered it was odd. Chopsticks weren't offered to us either, which was something I noticed about the few other white appearing families in the restaurant as well. Asian customers were all offered chopsticks to eat with, while all the white customers were handed forks without even a question. This isn't the worst thing in the world and maybe I should have asked, but it felt like there were assumptions being made and that made me uncomfortable.
And last but not least, I felt we were being rushed to leave from the moment we sat down. We were being checked on way too much to see if we were done with our plates yet, and they brought us our check before we had even finished.
Perhaps we came on an off day, but it was truly an unpleasant and unenjoyable experience for me, unfortunately, and this is not a restaurant I'll be eager to return to.</Review>

<Gmap_id>0x808e4030f9749301:0xfa816c089902aaa2<//Gmap_id><text>Shun Feng is a traditional family-style Chinese restaurant, complete with spinning center piece tables and all. I've been to a lot of Chinese restaurants all over the bay area, and this is definitely one of my favorites. Large menu with tons of options, and it's not too confusing (some pictures in the back) like some Asian restaurants can be. The food itself is served fresh and hot. Hunan beef, lemon or orange chicken, and honey walnut shrimp with house fried rice or wanton soup is always my go to. The meat is crispy and cooked well done, the sauce is great and the vegetables in the plates are a nice touch. I'm not a big fan of dim som, but my party usually orders it, and the bread is fluffy and moist. I usually even end up ordering some of the sesame balls with the sweet red paste filling as a dessert. Also very crispy, hot, and tasty. Its all moderately priced, so expect about 20-30$ for about two people (depending on how hungry you are.) All in all, the food here is great and the staff is friendly and quick. I haven't been to a better Asian restaurant in Santa Cruz. Shen Fung is my go-to for a dinner out with friends.<//text>< rate>

<Review>Came in after 8 so I can't blame them entirely, for not having any S&P shakers on the tables cuz they were all being washed.The restaurant was slow, but it seemed like a good place to get a late dinner. There were just a few people on staff and only a few customers in at this time.

I ordered a 55+ dinner of chicken fried steak and a green salad (cuz there was no soup), and I asked what came on it was told only tomato & red onion. I asked if there were any cucumbers I could but no. I conceded to ask for extra tomato, to which she complied. I asked about salad dressing and there were only 2 kinds & none of which was my preference... Blue Cheese. (I settled for Ranch on the side).

When the salad came tho, there were lots of RINGS of red onion laying on top & lots of bright red tomato wedges, which was really great to have. I did have to ask for a side plate so I could cut up the onions & cut the tomatoes smaller. I then asked if there were any croutons, expecting the answer would be "no" since they weren't on the salad already, but my server said there were, and she brought me a BAGGIE of croutons! LOL

The dinner arrived before I could finish my salad unfortunately, so I pushed away the side of cold food in lieu of the hot food that had just arrived. I opted to order it with a side of something called "red potato hash" instead of mashed potatoes (cuz mashed were powdered from a box). they brought me a side and gravy because I had asked for greeting to be put on top of it and it wasn't which was fine. The broccoli that I had was rather cold, but the chicken fried steak was huge! It was overcooked for my taste but I just finished half of it.

All in all, I guess it was an OK dinner for being here at IHOP because I was hungry oh, but I probably won't be back due to the limited selection they have on the 55+ dinner menu. One can't expect to have 5-star service necessarily in this type of establishment. It is what it is...& it filled the gut!< /Review>< user_name>

<review>Parking: Medium-sized lot that can fill up fast on the weekends.

Decor: Your bland corporate diner booths. Not very roomy. Overhead hanging light is too bright. At least it's clean.

<Pictures>None< /Pictures>< review>
One of my favorite all-time IHOPs anywhere in the country, and definitely best I've been to in Bay Area.  This location is in one  of the iconic IHOP blue peak-roof buildings, not one of the newer, plain jane ones, so immediately it's special.  Bright interior.  Serving staff -- at least at night when I usually go -- are awesome, especially Oscar.  Food is better here than the other IHOPs in South SF and Daly City -- good chef.  Again, I'm talking about night crew, never been here daytime.  Also, this location is open 24 hours on Fri & Sat nite, which is a big plus for me.</review>
